style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         Location\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         John F. Kennedy Space Center,\n         <a href="/wiki/Titusville,_Florida" title="Titusville, Florida">\n          Titusville, Florida\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         Area\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         7,000 acres (2,800\xc2\xa0ha)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         Built\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         1967\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiple_Property_Submission" title="Multiple Property Submission">\n          MPS\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         <a class="external text" href="http://focus.nps.gov/pdfhost/docs/NRHP/Text/64500111.pdf" rel="nofollow">\n          John F. Kennedy Space Center MPS\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         NRHP\xc2\xa0reference\xc2\xa0#\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         <a class="external text" href="https://npgallery.nps.gov/AssetDetail/NRIS/73000568" rel="nofollow">\n          73000568\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nris_1-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-nris-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="font-weight:bold; border: 0;">\n         Added to NRHP\n        </th>\n        <td style="border: 0;">\n         May 24, 1973\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Launch Complex 39 (LC-39)\n       </b>\n       is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rocket_launch_site" title="Rocket launch site">\n        rocket launch site\n       </a>\n       at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Space_Center" title="John F. Kennedy Space Center">\n        John F. Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a href="/wiki/Merritt_Island,_Florida" title="Merritt Island, Florida">\n        Merritt Island\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       , United States. The site and its collection of facilities were originally built for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       , and later modified for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       . As of 2017, only Launch Complex 39A is active, launching\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       . LC-39 is also being modified to support launches of the SpaceX\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n        Dragon 2\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Falcon Heavy\n       </a>\n       , as well as NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       , with a new, smaller pad, C, added to support smaller launches.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Launch Complex 39 is composed of three launch pads\xe2\x80\x94\n       <a href="#Launch_Pad_39A">\n        39A\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="#Launch_Pad_39B">\n        39B\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="#Launch_Pad_39C">\n        39C\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       (VAB), a\n       <a href="/wiki/Crawlerway" title="Crawlerway">\n        Crawlerway\n       </a>\n       used by\n       <a href="/wiki/Crawler-transporter" title="Crawler-transporter">\n        crawler-transporters\n       </a>\n       to carry\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Launcher_Platform" title="Mobile Launcher Platform">\n        Mobile Launcher Platforms\n       </a>\n       between the VAB and the pads,\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n        Orbiter Processing Facility\n       </a>\n       buildings, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n        Launch Control Center\n       </a>\n       which contains the firing rooms, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Complex_39_Press_Site" title="Launch Complex 39 Press Site">\n        news facility\n       </a>\n       famous for the iconic countdown clock seen in television coverage and photos, and various logistical and operational support buildings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX leases Launch Pad 39A from NASA and has modified the pad to support Falcon Heavy launches in 2017 and beyond.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       began modifying Launch Pad 39B in 2007 to accommodate the now defunct\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Constellation" title="Project Constellation">\n        Project Constellation\n       </a>\n       , and is currently preparing it for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pad1_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pad1-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pad2_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pad2-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with first launch scheduled for 2018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Pad C was originally planned but never built for Apollo, and would have been a copy of pads 39A and 39B. A smaller pad, designated 39C was constructed from January to June 2015 to accommodate\n       <a href="/wiki/Small-lift_launch_vehicle" title="Small-lift launch vehicle">\n        small-class vehicles.\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA launches from LC-39A and 39B have been supervised from the NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n        Launch Control Center\n       </a>\n       (LCC), located 3 miles (4.8\xc2\xa0km) from the launch pads. LC-39 is one of several launch sites that share radar and tracking services of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Test_Range" title="Eastern Test Range">\n        Eastern Test Range\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n         </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Constellation_Program_and_Pad_39B">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.4\n            </span>\n 2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Launch Pad 39A\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#Launch_Pad_39B">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Launch Pad 39B\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Launch_Pad_39C">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Launch Pad 39C\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-29">\n             <a           </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-30">\n             <a href="#Capabilities_2">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.3.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Capabilities\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n   <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">\n        Early history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Northern Merritt Island was first developed around 1890 when a few wealthy Harvard University graduates purchased 18,000 acres (73\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) and constructed a three-story mahogany clubhouse, very nearly on the site of Pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the 1920s, Peter E. Studebaker Jr., son of\n       <a href="/wiki/Studebaker" title="Studebaker">\n        the automobile magnate\n       </a>\n       , built a small casino at De Soto Beach eight miles (13\xc2\xa0km) north of the Canaveral lighthouse.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1948, the Navy transferred the former Banana River Naval Air Station located south of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">\n        Cape Canaveral\n       </a>\n       , to the Air Force for use in testing captured German V-2 rockets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The site\'s location on the East Florida coast was ideal for this purpose in that launches would be over the ocean, away from populated areas. This site became the Joint Long Range Proving Ground in 1949, and was renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Air_Force_Base" title="Patrick Air Force Base">\n        Patrick Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       in 1950. The Air Force annexed part of Cape Canaveral to the North in 1951, forming the Air Force Missile Test Center, the future\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       (CCAFS). Missile and rocketry testing and development would take place here through the 1950s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Creation_of_NASA" title="Creation of NASA">\n        creation of NASA\n       </a>\n       in 1958, the CCAFS launch pads were used for NASA\'s civilian unmanned and manned launches, including those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Mercury" title="Project Mercury">\n        Project Mercury\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Gemini" title="Project Gemini">\n        Project Gemini\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Apollo_and_Skylab">\n        Apollo and Skylab\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Apollo and Skylab">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_program.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="619" data-file-width="619" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo_program.svg/220px-Apollo_program.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo_program.svg/330px-Apollo_program.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Apollo_program.svg/440px-Apollo_program.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_program.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Apollo Program\'s patch\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1961, President Kennedy proposed to Congress the goal of landing a man on the Moon by the end of the decade. Congressional approval led to the launch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">\n        Apollo program\n       </a>\n       , which required a massive expansion of NASA operations, including an expansion of launch operations from the Cape to adjacent Merritt Island to the north and west.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA began acquisition of land in 1962, taking title to 131 square miles (340\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) by outright purchase and negotiating with the state of Florida for an additional 87 square miles (230\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). On July 1, 1962, the site was named the\n       <b>\n        Launch Operations Center\n       </b>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_design">\n        Initial design\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Initial design">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:542px;max-width:542px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:338px;max-width:338px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:252px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="658" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png/336px-Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png/504px-Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Lc39_plan_1963_labelled.png 2x" width="336"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Launch Complex Plan \xe2\x80\x93 1963\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:200px;max-width:200px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:252px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1410" data-file-width="1107" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg/198px-Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg/297px-Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg/396px-Lc39_warning_lamps.jpg 2x" width="198"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Warning lamps for the planned 3 pads, including the unbuilt pad C\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       At the time, the highest numbered launch pad on CCAFS was Launch Complex 37; when the lunar launch complex was designed, it was designated as Launch Complex 39. It was designed to handle launches of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn\xc2\xa0V\n       </a>\n       rocket, at the time the largest, most powerful rocket then designed, required to take Apollo to the Moon. Initial plans included four pads (five were considered) evenly spaced 8,700 feet (2,700\xc2\xa0m) apart to avoid damage in the event of an explosion on the pad. Three were scheduled for construction (A-C, to the southeast) and two (D and E, west and north) would have been built at a later date. The numbering of the pads at the time was from north to south, with the northernmost being 39A, and the southernmost being 39C. Pad 39A was never built, and 39C became 39A in 1963. With today\'s numbering, 39C would have been north of 39B, and 39D would have been due west of 39C. Pad 39E would have been due north of the mid-distance between 39C and 39D, with 39E forming the top of a triangle, and equidistant from 39C and 39D. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Crawlerway" title="Crawlerway">\n        Crawlerway\n       </a>\n       was built with the additional pads in mind. This is the reason the Crawlerway turns as it heads to Pad\xc2\xa0B; continuing straight from that turn would have led to the additional pads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Integration_of_space_vehicle_stack">\n        Integration of space vehicle stack\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Integration of space vehicle stack">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;max-width:272px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:204px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="917" data-file-width="1200" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg/268px-69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg/402px-69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg/536px-69-HC-620_-_SA506.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Apollo-Saturn 506 with\n          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">\n           Apollo 11\n          </a>\n          spacecraft being moved from the VAB to LC39A (1969)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:178px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crawler-Transporter.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1993" data-file-width="3000" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/268px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/402px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crawler-Transporter.jpg/536px-Crawler-Transporter.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          A restored Crawler-Transporter (2004)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Months before launch, the three stages of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n        Saturn V\n       </a>\n       launch vehicle and the components of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo_spacecraft" title="Apollo spacecraft">\n        Apollo spacecraft\n       </a>\n       were brought inside the Vehicle Assembly Building (VAB) and assembled in one of four high bays into a 363-foot (111\xc2\xa0m)-tall space vehicle on one of three\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Launcher_Platform" title="Mobile Launcher Platform">\n        Mobile Launchers\n       </a>\n       . Each mobile launcher consisted of a two-story, 161-by-135-foot (49 by 41\xc2\xa0m) launch platform with four hold-down arms and a 446-foot (136\xc2\xa0m) Launch Umbilical Tower (LUT) topped by a crane used to lift the spacecraft into position for assembly. The MLP and unfueled vehicle together weighed 12,600,000 pounds (5,715\xc2\xa0t).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Umbilical Tower contained two elevators and nine retractable swing arms which extended to the space vehicle, to provide access to each of the three rocket stages and the spacecraft for people, wiring and plumbing while the vehicle was on the launch pad, and swung away from the vehicle at launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Technicians, engineers, and astronauts used the uppermost Spacecraft Access Arm to access the crew cabin. At the end of the arm, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_room_(spacecraft)" title="White room (spacecraft)">\n        white room\n       </a>\n       provided an environmentally controlled and protected area for astronauts and their equipment to enter the spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_to_the_pad">\n        Transportation to the pad\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Transportation to the pad">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       When the stack integration was completed, it was moved the 3\xe2\x80\x934 miles (4.8\xe2\x80\x936.4\xc2\xa0km) to the pad at a speed of 1 mile (1.6\xc2\xa0km) per hour by one of two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crawler-Transporter" title="Crawler-Transporter">\n        Crawler-Transporters\n       </a>\n       . Each crawler weighed 6,000,000 pounds (2,720\xc2\xa0t) and was capable of keeping the space vehicle on its Mobile Launcher level while negotiating a 5 percent grade to the pad. At the pad, the MLP was supported by six steel pedestals, plus four additional extensible columns.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_Service_Structure">\n        Mobile Service Structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mobile Service Structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="1508" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cd/Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg/200px-Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cd/Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg/300px-Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cd/Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg/400px-Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saturn_V_and_service_structures.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n          Saturn V\n         </a>\n         with fixed (left) and mobile (right) service structures\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LC-39A_walkway.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/LC-39A_walkway.jpg/200px-LC-39A_walkway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/LC-39A_walkway.jpg/300px-LC-39A_walkway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/LC-39A_walkway.jpg/400px-LC-39A_walkway.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LC-39A_walkway.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Apollo-era walkway and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_room_(spaceflight)" title="White room (spaceflight)">\n          white room\n         </a>\n         , on display at\n         <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">\n          Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After the MLP was set in place, the Crawler-Transporter rolled a 410-foot (125\xc2\xa0m), 10,490,000-pound (4,760\xc2\xa0t) Mobile\n       <a href="/wiki/Service_structure" title="Service structure">\n        Service Structure\n       </a>\n       (MSS) into place to provide further access for technicians to perform detailed checkout of the vehicle, and necessary umbillical connections to the pad. The MSS contained three elevators, two self-propelled platforms and three fixed platforms, and was rolled back 6,900 feet (2,100\xc2\xa0m) to its parking position shortly before launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flame_deflector">\n        Flame deflector\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flame deflector">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       A flame deflector was slid on rails into place under the launch pedestal. This system allowed for rotation with a second flame deflector, after the first was refurbished after each launch. Each deflector measured 39 feet (12\xc2\xa0m) high by 49 feet (15\xc2\xa0m) wide by 75 feet (23\xc2\xa0m) long and weighed 1,400,000 pounds (635\xc2\xa0t). It deflected the exhaust flame into a trench measuring 43 feet (13\xc2\xa0m) deep by 59 feet (18\xc2\xa0m) wide by 449 feet (137\xc2\xa0m) long.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_control_and_fueling">\n        Launch control and fueling\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Launch control and fueling">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The four-story\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n        Launch Control Center\n       </a>\n       was located 3.5 miles (5.6\xc2\xa0km) away from Pad A, adjacent to the Vehicle Assembly Building for safety. The third floor had four firing rooms (corresponding to the four high bays in the VAB), each with 470 sets of control and monitoring equipment.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2014)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The second floor contained telemetry, tracking, instrumentation, and data reduction computing equipment. The LCC was connected to the Mobile Launchers by a high speed data link, and during launch a system of 62 closed-circuit television cameras transmitted to 100 monitor screens in the LCC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Large cryogenic tanks located near the pads stored the liquid hydrogen and liquid oxygen (LOX) for the second and third stages of the Saturn V. The highly explosive nature of these chemicals required numerous safety measures at the Launch Complex. The pads were located 8,730 feet (2,660\xc2\xa0m) away from each other.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moonport_appendixb_17-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Moonport_appendixb-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before tanking operations began and during launch, non-essential personnel were excluded from the danger area.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_evacuation_system">\n        Emergency evacuation system\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Emergency evacuation system">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Each pad had a 200-foot (61\xc2\xa0m) evacuation tube running from the Mobile Launcher platform to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rubber_room_(bunker)" title="Rubber room (bunker)">\n        blast-resistant bunker\n       </a>\n       39 feet (12\xc2\xa0m) underground, equipped with survival supplies for 20 persons for 24 hours. There was also a cab/slidewire system running from the 322-foot (98\xc2\xa0m) tower level to evacuate astronauts and technicians 2,503 feet (763\xc2\xa0m) away from the pad.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pad_Terminal_Connection_Room">\n        Pad Terminal Connection Room\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Pad Terminal Connection Room">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Connections between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_Control_Center" title="Launch Control Center">\n        Launch Control Center\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_launcher_platform" title="Mobile launcher platform">\n        mobile launcher platform\n       </a>\n       and space vehicle are made in the Pad Terminal Connection Room (PTCR). The facility was a two-story series of rooms beneath the launch pad, constructed of reinforced concrete located on the west side of the flame trench and was protected by up to 20 feet (6.1\xc2\xa0m) of fill dirt.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Apollo_and_Skylab_launches">\n        Apollo and Skylab launches\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Apollo and Skylab launches">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;max-width:272px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:343px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Apollo4.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="798" height="344" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Launch_Apollo4.jpg/268px-Launch_Apollo4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Launch_Apollo4.jpg/402px-Launch_Apollo4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Launch_Apollo4.jpg/536px-Launch_Apollo4.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <a href="/wiki/Apollo_4" title="Apollo 4">\n           Apollo 4\n          </a>\n          , the first unmanned test flight of the\n          <a href="/wiki/Saturn_V" title="Saturn V">\n           Saturn V\n          </a>\n          , rising from pad 39A (November 1967)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage" style="height:214px;overflow:hidden">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg/268px-ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg/402px-ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg/536px-ASTP_Launch_-_GPN-2000-000643.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Final launch of\n          <a href="/wiki/Saturn_IB" title="Saturn IB">\n           Saturn IB\n          </a>\n          from pad 39B, carrying the\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo-Soyuz Test Project">\n           Apollo-Soyuz Test Project\n          </a>\n          Command Module into orbit (July 1975)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first use of LC-39 came in 1967 with the first Saturn\xc2\xa0V launch, carrying the unmanned\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_4" title="Apollo 4">\n        Apollo\xc2\xa04\n       </a>\n       spacecraft. The second unmanned launch,\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_6" title="Apollo 6">\n        Apollo\xc2\xa06\n       </a>\n       , also used Pad 39A. With the exception of\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">\n        Apollo\xc2\xa010\n       </a>\n       , which used Pad 39B (due to the "all-up" testing resulting in a 2-month turnaround period), all manned Apollo-Saturn\xc2\xa0V launches, commencing with\n       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">\n        Apollo\xc2\xa08\n       </a>\n       , used Pad 39A.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A total of thirteen Saturn Vs were launched for Apollo, and the unmanned launch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       space station in 1973. The mobile launchers were then modified for the shorter\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_IB" title="Saturn IB">\n        Saturn IB\n       </a>\n       rockets, by adding a "milk-stool" extension platform to the launch pedestal, so that the\n       <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">\n        S-IVB\n       </a>\n       upper stage and Apollo spacecraft swing arms would reach. These were used for three manned Skylab flights and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo-Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo-Soyuz Test Project\n       </a>\n       , since the Saturn IB pads 34 and 37 at Cape Canaveral AFB had been decommissioned.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Space Shuttle">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The thrust to allow the Space Shuttle to achieve orbit was provided by a combination of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        Solid Rocket Boosters\n       </a>\n       (SRBs) and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Main_Engine" title="Space Shuttle Main Engine">\n        Space Shuttle Main Engines\n       </a>\n       (SSMEs). The SRBs used solid propellant, hence their name. The SSMEs used a combination of\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrogen" title="Liquid hydrogen">\n        liquid hydrogen\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_oxygen" title="Liquid oxygen">\n        liquid oxygen\n       </a>\n       (LOX) from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_Tank" title="External Tank">\n        External Tank\n       </a>\n       (ET), as the orbiter did not have internal fuel tanks for the SSMEs (as they would be have had to be as large as the External Tank). The SRBs arrived in segments via rail car from their manufacturing facility in\n       <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">\n        Utah\n       </a>\n       , the External Tank arrived from its manufacturing facility in\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       by barge, and the orbiter waited in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Processing_Facility" title="Orbiter Processing Facility">\n        Orbiter Processing Facility\n       </a>\n       (OPF). The SRBs were first stacked in the VAB, and then the External Tank was mounted between them. Then, using a massive crane, the orbiter was lowered and connected to the External Tank.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Payload to be installed at the launch pad was independently transported in a payload transportation canister then installed vertically at the Payload Changeout Room. Otherwise, payloads would have already been pre-installed at the Orbiter Processing Facility and transported within the orbiter\'s cargo bay.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The original structure of the pads was remodeled for the needs of the Space Shuttle, starting with Pad 39A after the last Saturn\xc2\xa0V launch, and in 1977 for Pad 39B after the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Apollo-Soyuz Test Project">\n        Apollo-Soyuz Test Project\n       </a>\n       in 1975.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3000" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg/240px-Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg/360px-Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg/480px-Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg 2x" width="240"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbia.sts-1.01.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n          <i>\n           Columbia\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         standing on pad 39A, ready for its first orbital flight (\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n          STS-1\n         </a>\n         , April 1981). The Rotating Service Structure has been rolled away in preparation for launch.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_towers">\n        Launch towers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Launch towers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Each pad contained a two-piece access tower system, the Fixed Service Structure (FSS) and the Rotating Service Structure (RSS). The FSS permitted access to the Shuttle via a retractable arm and a "beanie cap" to capture vented LOX from the External Tank. The RSS contained the Payload Changeout Room, which offered "clean" access to the orbiter\'s payload bay, protection from the elements, and protection in winds up to 60 knots (110\xc2\xa0km/h).\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sound_suppression_water_system">\n        Sound suppression water system\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sound suppression water system">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       A Sound Suppression Water System (SSWS) was added to protect the Space Shuttle and its payload from effects of the intense sound wave pressure generated by its engines. An elevated water tank on a 290-foot (88\xc2\xa0m) tower near each pad stored 300,000 gallons (1.1\xc2\xa0Megalitres) of water, which was released onto the Mobile Launcher Platform just before engine ignition.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_suppression_system_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_suppression_system-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The water muffled the intense sound waves produced by the engines. Due to heating of the water, a large quantity of steam was produced during launch.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Swing_arm_modifications">\n        Swing arm modifications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Swing arm modifications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2008" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg/200px-Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg/300px-Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg/400px-Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Pad_39A_KSC_White_Room_Access_Arm_Walkway.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The doors to the White Room, which provided entry to the Shuttle crew compartment, are seen here at the end of the access arm walkway\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Gaseous Oxygen Vent Arm positioned a hood, often called the "Beanie Cap," over the top of the External Tank (ET) nose cone during fueling.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (February 2014)">\n           when?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Heated gaseous nitrogen was used there to remove the extremely cold gaseous oxygen that normally vented out of the External Tank. This prevented the formation of ice that could fall and damage the shuttle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Hydrogen Vent Line Access Arm mated the External Tank (ET)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_Umbilical_Carrier_Plate" title="Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate">\n        Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate\n       </a>\n       (GUCP) to the launch pad hydrogen vent line. The GUCP provided support for plumbing and cables, called umbilicals, that transferred fluids, gases, and electrical signals between two pieces of equipment. While the ET was being fueled, hazardous gas was vented from an internal hydrogen tank through the GUCP, out a vent line to a flare stack where it was burned off at a safe distance. Sensors at the GUCP measured gas level. The GUCP was redesigned after leaks created scrubs of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">\n        STS-127\n       </a>\n       and were also detected during attempts to launch\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-119" title="STS-119">\n        STS-119\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">\n        STS-133\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The GUCP released from the ET at launch and fell away with a curtain of water sprayed across it for protection from flames.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_pad_evacuation">\n        Emergency pad evacuation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Emergency pad evacuation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Astroescape.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Astroescape.jpg/200px-Astroescape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Astroescape.jpg/300px-Astroescape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Astroescape.jpg/400px-Astroescape.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Astroescape.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         M113 armored personnel carriers parked near LC-39\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In an emergency, the launch complex used a slidewire escape basket system for quick evacuation. Assisted by members of the closeout team, the crew would leave the orbiter and ride an emergency basket to the ground at speeds reaching up to 55 miles per hour (89\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronaut_rescue_drill_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astronaut_rescue_drill-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       From there, the crew took shelter in a bunker. A modified\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M113_Armored_Personnel_Carrier" title="M113 Armored Personnel Carrier">\n        M113 Armored Personnel Carrier\n       </a>\n       could carry injured astronauts away from the complex to safety.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astronaut_evacuation_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-astronaut_evacuation-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the launch of Discovery on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-124" title="STS-124">\n        STS-124\n       </a>\n       on May\xc2\xa031, 2008, the pad at LC-39A suffered extensive damage, in particular to the concrete trench used to deflect the SRB\'s flames.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-damage_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-damage-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The subsequent mishap investigation found that the damage was the result of carbonation of epoxy and corrosion of steel anchors which held the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refractory_brick" title="Refractory brick">\n        refractory bricks\n       </a>\n       in the trench in place. These had been exacerbated by the fact that\n       <a href="/wiki/Hydrochloric_acid" title="Hydrochloric acid">\n        hydrochloric acid\n       </a>\n       is an exhaust by-product of the solid rocket boosters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Shuttle_launches">\n        Space Shuttle launches\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Space Shuttle launches">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       After the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       in 1973, Pad 39A was reconfigured for the Space Shuttle, with shuttle launches beginning in 1981 with\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n        STS-1\n       </a>\n       , flown by the\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mods_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mods-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After Apollo\xc2\xa010, Pad 39B was kept as a backup launch facility in the case of the destruction of 39A, but saw service for all three Skylab missions, the Apollo-Soyuz test flight, and a contingency Skylab Rescue flight that never became necessary. After the Apollo-Soyuz Test Project, 39B was reconfigured similarly to 39A, but due to additional modifications (mainly to allow the facility to service a modified\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centaur_(rocket)" title="Centaur (rocket)">\n        Centaur-G\n       </a>\n       upper stage), along with budgetary restraints, it was not ready until 1986, and the first shuttle flight to use it was\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">\n        STS-51-L\n       </a>\n       , which ended with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">\n        <i>\n         Challenger\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       . The first return to flight mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-26" title="STS-26">\n        STS-26\n       </a>\n       launched from 39B.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constellation_Program_and_Pad_39B">\n        Constellation Program and Pad 39B\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Constellation Program and Pad 39B">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="1996" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/170px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/255px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg/340px-Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ares_I-X_launch_08.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ares I-X launches from LC-39B, 15:30 UTC, October\xc2\xa028, 2009\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The last Shuttle launch from Pad 39B was the nighttime launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n        STS-116\n       </a>\n       on December 9, 2006. To support the final Shuttle mission to the Hubble Space Telescope\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       launched from Pad 39A in May 2009,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         Endeavour\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was placed on 39B if needed to launch the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-400" title="STS-400">\n        STS-400\n       </a>\n       rescue mission.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After the completion of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       , 39B was converted for the single test flight of the\n       <i>\n        Constellation Program\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I-X" title="Ares I-X">\n        Ares\xc2\xa0I-X\n       </a>\n       from Pad 39B on October\xc2\xa028, 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="2011\xe2\x80\x932013">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.932013">\n        2011\xe2\x80\x932013\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2011\xe2\x80\x932013">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       With the retirement of the Shuttle in 2011,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bw20101028_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bw20101028-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the cancellation of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellation_Program" title="Constellation Program">\n        Constellation Program\n       </a>\n       in 2010, the future of the LC-39 pads was uncertain. By early 2011, NASA began informal discussions on use of the pads and facilities by\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        private companies\n       </a>\n       to fly missions for the commercial space market,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft20110206_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ft20110206-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       culminating in a 20-year lease agreement with SpaceX for Pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flortoda_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-flortoda-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pad_39A">\n        Pad 39A\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pad 39A">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Just like the first 24 shuttle flights, Pad 39A supported the final manifested shuttle flights, starting with\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-117" title="STS-117">\n        STS-117\n       </a>\n       in June 2007 until the retirement of the shuttle fleet in July 2011. Prior to the SpaceX lease agreement, the pad remained as it was when Atlantis launched on the final shuttle mission on July 8, 2011, complete with a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_launcher_platform" title="Mobile launcher platform">\n        mobile launcher platform\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2689" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg/220px-PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg/330px-PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg/440px-PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PAD_39A_lease_announcement.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         KSC Director\n         <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Cabana" title="Robert D. Cabana">\n          Bob Cabana\n         </a>\n         announces the signing of the pad 39A lease agreement on April 14, 2014.\n         <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n          SpaceX\n         </a>\n         COO\n         <a href="/wiki/Gwynne_Shotwell" title="Gwynne Shotwell">\n          Gwynne Shotwell\n         </a>\n         stands nearby.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Talks for use of the pad were underway between NASA and\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Florida" title="Space Florida">\n        Space Florida\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Florida" title="State of Florida">\n        State of Florida\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_development_agency" title="Economic development agency">\n        economic development agency\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94as early as 2011, but no deal materialized by 2012 and NASA then pursued other options for removing the pad from the Federal government inventory.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20141117_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20141117-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By early 2013, NASA publicly announced that it would allow commercial launch providers to lease Pad 39A,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and followed that, in May 2013, with a formal solicitation for proposals for\n       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">\n        commercial use\n       </a>\n       of Launch Pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsw20130520_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsw20130520-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There were two competing bids for the commercial use of the launch complex.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leasedoc_40-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leasedoc-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       submitted a bid for exclusive use of the launch complex, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">\n        Jeff Bezos\n       </a>\n       \'\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Origin" title="Blue Origin">\n        Blue Origin\n       </a>\n       submitted a bid for shared non-exclusive use of the complex such that the launchpad would interface with multiple vehicles, and costs could be shared over the long term. One potential shared user in the Blue Origin plan was\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Launch_Alliance" title="United Launch Alliance">\n        United Launch Alliance\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-os20130818_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-os20130818-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prior to completion of the bid period, and prior to any public announcement by NASA of the results of the process, Blue Origin filed a protest with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n        U.S.\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Accounting_Office" title="General Accounting Office">\n        General Accounting Office\n       </a>\n       (GAO) "over what it says is a plan by NASA to award an exclusive commercial lease to SpaceX for use of mothballed space shuttle launch pad 39A."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pa20130910_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pa20130910-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA had planned to complete the bid award and have the pad transferred by October 1, 2013, but the protest "will delay any decision until the GAO reaches a decision, expected by mid-December."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pa20130910_42-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pa20130910-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On December 12, 2013, the GAO denied the protest and sided with NASA, which argued that the solicitation contains no preference on the use of the facility as multi-use or single-use. "The [solicitation] document merely asks bidders to explain their reasons for selecting one approach instead of the other and how they would manage the facility."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pa20131212_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pa20131212-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On December 13, 2013, NASA announced that they had selected SpaceX as the new commercial tenant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-padnego_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-padnego-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX signed the lease agreement on April 14, 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flortoda_36-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-flortoda-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They have been given a twenty-year exclusive lease of Pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leasedoc_40-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leasedoc-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX plans to launch their\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Falcon Heavy\n       </a>\n       from the pad and build a new hangar near it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leasedoc_40-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leasedoc-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flortoda_36-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-flortoda-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tss20140321_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tss20140321-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">\n        Elon Musk\n       </a>\n       , CEO of SpaceX, has stated that he wants to shift most of their NASA launches to Pad 39A, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Cargo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Development" title="Commercial Crew Development">\n        Crew\n       </a>\n       missions to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-padnego_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-padnego-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_status">\n        Current status\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Current status">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="1280" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg/240px-LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg/360px-LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg/480px-LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg 2x" width="240"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LC39A_and_LC39B.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The aerial view of both launch pads at the complex, 39A (foreground) and 39B\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_Pad_39A">\n        Launch Pad 39A\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Launch Pad 39A">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Complex_39A.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Launch_Complex_39A.JPG/220px-Launch_Complex_39A.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Launch_Complex_39A.JPG 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Complex_39A.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39A\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On April 14, 2014, the privately owned launch service provider\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       signed a 20-year lease for Launch Pad 39A.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The pad was modified to support launches of both\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9" title="Falcon 9">\n        Falcon 9\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Falcon Heavy\n       </a>\n       launch vehicles, which included the construction of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_Integration_Facility" title="Horizontal Integration Facility">\n        horizontal integration facility\n       </a>\n       , similar to that used at existing SpaceX-leased facilities at\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral_Air_Force_Station" title="Cape Canaveral Air Force Station">\n        Cape Canaveral Air Force Station\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Vandenberg_Air_Force_Base" title="Vandenberg Air Force Base">\n        Vandenberg Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 this is a marked difference from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        vertical integration\n       </a>\n       process used by NASA\'s own Apollo and Space Shuttle vehicles at the Launch Complex 39. Additionally new instrumentation and control systems were installed, and substantial new plumbing was added for a variety of rocket liquids and gasses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft20140414_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ft20140414-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_and_first_launch">\n        Construction and first launch\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Construction and first launch">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;max-width:272px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/SpaceX_HIF_at_KSC_LC-39A_%2827550168066%29.jpg/402px-SpaceX_HIF_at_KSC_LC-39A_%2827550168066%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/SpaceX_HIF_at_KSC_LC-39A_%2827550168066%29.jpg/536px-SpaceX_HIF_at_KSC_LC-39A_%2827550168066%29.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          SpaceX Horizontal Integration Facility (HIF)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle"
