SpaceX CRS-10\n          </a>\n          mission lifts off to the International Space Station (February 2017)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:270px;max-width:270px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_(26428480464).jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg/268px-Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg/402px-Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg/536px-Landed_rockets_in_hangar_39A_%2826428480464%29.jpg 2x" width="268"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Falcon 9 first-stage boosters\n          <a href="/wiki/Falcon_9_first-stage_landing_tests" title="Falcon 9 first-stage landing tests">\n           recovered after landing\n          </a>\n          (inside the HIF, May 2016)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2015, SpaceX built a large\n       <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_Integration_Facility" title="Horizontal Integration Facility">\n        Horizontal Integration Facility\n       </a>\n       (HIF) just outside the perimeter of the existing launch pad in order to house both the Falcon 9, and the Falcon Heavy, rockets, and their associated hardware and payloads, during preparation for flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20150225_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20150225-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Both types of launch vehicles will be transported from the HIF to the launch pad aboard a Transporter Erector (TE) which will ride on rails up the former Crawlerway path.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20141117_37-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20141117-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20150225_50-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20150225-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also in 2015, the launch mount for the Falcon Heavy was constructed on Pad 39A over the existing infrastructure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cs20140414_51-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cs20140414-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The work on both the HIF building, and the pad, were substantially complete by late 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20151008_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20151008-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A rollout test of the new Transporter/Erector (TE) was conducted in November 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20151109_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20151109-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX indicated in February 2016 that they had "completed and activated Launch Complex 39A",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20160204_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20160204-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but still has more work yet to do to support crewed flights. SpaceX originally planned to be ready to accomplish the first launch at pad 39A \xe2\x80\x94 a Falcon Heavy \xe2\x80\x94 as early as 2015,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ft20140414_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ft20140414-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as they had architects and engineers working on the new design and modifications since 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cs20140414_51-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cs20140414-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By late 2014, a preliminary date for a\n       <a href="/wiki/Wet_dress_rehearsal" title="Wet dress rehearsal">\n        wet dress rehearsal\n       </a>\n       of the Falcon Heavy was set for no earlier than July 1, 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20141117_37-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20141117-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to a failure in a June 2015 Falcon 9 launch, SpaceX had to delay launching the Falcon Heavy in order to focus on the Falcon 9\'s failure investigation and its return to flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In early 2016, considering the busy Falcon 9 launch manifest, it became unclear if Falcon Heavy would be the first vehicle to launch from Pad 39A, or if one or more Falcon 9 missions would precede a Falcon Heavy launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20160204_55-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sn20160204-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first SpaceX launch from pad 39A was\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-10" title="SpaceX CRS-10">\n        SpaceX CRS-10\n       </a>\n       using a Falcon 9 on February 19, 2017; it was the company\'s 10th cargo resupply mission to the International Space Station,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the first unmanned launch from 39A since Skylab.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_flights">\n        Future flights\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Future flights">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       As a result of ongoing reconstruction at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SLC-40" title="SLC-40">\n        SLC-40\n       </a>\n       after the loss of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AMOS-6" title="AMOS-6">\n        AMOS-6\n       </a>\n       satellite, all SpaceX\'s east coast launches are being launched from LC-39A until SLC-40 is back to operational status (currently scheduled for no earlier than December of 2017). On May 1, 2017,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NROL" title="NROL">\n        NROL\n       </a>\n       -76 was the first SpaceX mission for the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Reconnaissance_Office" title="National Reconnaissance Office">\n        National Reconnaissance Office\n       </a>\n       with a classified payload.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Future notable missions include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n         Falcon Heavy\n        </a>\n        Demo: 4th Quarter 2017; LC-39A; with two reused side boosters.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_60-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-:2-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Futurism_61-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Futurism-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n         Dragon 2\n        </a>\n        : planned for launch in February 2018. This would be the first launch of this vehicle, and will be unmanned.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A second Dragon 2 mission scheduled for mid-2018 will launch the first crewed mission from LC-39A and the United States since\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-135" title="STS-135">\n         STS-135\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Private manned mission with\n        <a href="/wiki/Dragon_2" title="Dragon 2">\n         Dragon 2\n        </a>\n        around the Moon, end of 2018; Falcon Heavy.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_62-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-:0-62">\n          [62]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Capabilities">\n        Capabilities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Capabilities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       SpaceX intends to utilize the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fixed_Service_Structure" title="Fixed Service Structure">\n        Fixed Service Structure\n       </a>\n       (FSS) of the Pad 39A\n       <a href="#Launch_towers">\n        launch towers\n       </a>\n       , and will extend it above its existing 350-foot (110\xc2\xa0m) height, but will not need the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotating_Service_Structure" title="Rotating Service Structure">\n        Rotating Service Structure\n       </a>\n       (RSS) thus will remove it. Initial plans in 2014 called for leaving the RSS in place until after the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">\n        Falcon Heavy\n       </a>\n       launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20141117_37-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20141117-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, plans were changed since then, and work on RSS takedown began in February 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ses20141021_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ses20141021-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA has already removed the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbiter_Servicing_Arm" title="Orbiter Servicing Arm">\n        Orbiter Servicing Arm\n       </a>\n       - with intent to use the space later to build a museum - and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_room_(spaceflight)" title="White room (spaceflight)">\n        white room\n       </a>\n       by which astronauts entered the Space Shuttle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cs20140414_51-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cs20140414-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX indicated in late 2014 that no additional levels to the FSS would be added in the near term.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20141117_37-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20141117-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       fSpaceX plans to later add at least two additional levels to the FSS, and will utilize the FSS for providing\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        crew\n       </a>\n       access for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_V2" title="Dragon V2">\n        Dragon V2\n       </a>\n       launches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20140728_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20140728-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Launch vehicles will be assembled horizontally in a hangar near the pad, transferred to the pad, and then lifted atop a launch platform for the remainder of the launch prep and lift off.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        military\n       </a>\n       missions from Pad 39A,\n       <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">\n        payloads\n       </a>\n       will be vertically integrated, as that is required per launch contract with the US Air Force.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hammerhead_crane" title="Hammerhead crane">\n        hammerhead crane\n       </a>\n       is planned to be added to the FSS in order to support US military requirements for vertical payload integration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20140728_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20140728-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Pad 39A will be used to host launches of astronauts on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dragon_V2" title="Dragon V2">\n        crewed\n       </a>\n       -version of the\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon space capsule\n       </a>\n       in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public\xe2\x80\x93private partnership">\n        public\xe2\x80\x93private partnership\n       </a>\n       with NASA. The NASA plan as of April 2014\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       calls for the first NASA crewed missions in 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SpaceX intends to add "a crew gantry access arm and white room to allow for crew and cargo ingress to the vehicle. The existing Space Shuttle evacuation slide-wire basket system will also be re-purposed to provide a safe emergency egress for the Dragon crew in the event of an emergency on the pad that does not necessitate using the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crew_Dragon" title="Crew Dragon">\n        Crew Dragon\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x99s launch abort system."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20150227_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sx20150227-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_Pad_39B">\n        Launch Pad 39B\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Launch Pad 39B">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Complex_39B.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Launch_Complex_39B.JPG/220px-Launch_Complex_39B.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Launch_Complex_39B.JPG 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Launch_Complex_39B.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39B\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since the Ares I-X flight, NASA proceeded with plans to strip Pad 39B of its Flight Service Structure (FSS), returning the location to an Apollo-like "clean pad" design for the first time since 1977. This approach will make the pad available to multiple types of vehicles which arrive at the pad with service structures on the mobile launcher platform as opposed to custom structures on the pad.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The LH\n       <sub>\n        2\n       </sub>\n       , LOX, and water tanks (used for the sound suppression system) are the only structures left from the Space Shuttle era.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20150322_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20150322-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sound_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sound-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of June 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , repairs and modifications to selected facility systems at Launch Complex (LC) 39B for\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       (SLS) processing and launch operations are finishing the first phase of a five-phase project. The second phase of this project is currently budgeted at $89.2 million ($6.1 million in FY 2012, $28.5 million in FY 2013, $9.4 million in FY 2014 and $45.2 million in the outyears).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Precise_language" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">\n          <span title="The text near this tag is dated.">\n           needs update\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In March 2015, Pad 39B was undergoing modifications to the Catacomb Roof structure so that it can handle the loads from the SLS Block 1B rocket, increasing the load capacity to support the crawler-transporter and vertical rocket from 21,000,000 to 25,500,000 pounds (9,500,000 to 11,600,000\xc2\xa0kg).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsf20150322_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nsf20150322-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2014, NASA announced that it would make Pad 39B available to commercial users during times when it is not needed by the Space Launch System.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of May 2017\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , NASA has one SLS mission scheduled in 2019, and a second one in 2021.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfn20140415_56-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfn20140415-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_Pad_39C">\n        Launch Pad 39C\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Launch Pad 39C">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Launch Pad 39C is a new facility for\n       <a href="/wiki/Small-lift_launch_vehicle" title="Small-lift launch vehicle">\n        smaller launch vehicles\n       </a>\n       built in 2015 within the Launch Complex 39B perimeter.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">\n        Construction\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Construction">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       Construction of the pad began in January 2015 and was completed in June 2015.\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       Director\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Cabana" title="Robert D. Cabana">\n        Robert D. Cabana\n       </a>\n       and representatives from the Ground Systems Development and Operations (GSDO) Program and the Center Planning and Development (CPD) and Engineering Directorates marked the completion of the new pad during a ribbon-cutting ceremony July 17, 2015.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       "As America\'s premier spaceport, we\'re always looking for new and innovative ways to meet America\'s launch needs, and one area that was missing was small class\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payloads" title="Payloads">\n        payloads\n       </a>\n       ,"\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Cabana" title="Robert D. Cabana">\n        Robert D. Cabana\n       </a>\n       said. "Using 21st Century funds, we built Pad 39C."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       GSDO oversaw the project and is working with CPD to grow commercial space efforts at Kennedy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       "Pad 39C is the latest addition to our portfolio of launch pads," said Scott Colloredo, CPD director. "The small class market is here. The demand for that kind of launcher is increasing. The key here is this is really what a launch site for a small class launcher needs to look like."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The concrete pad measures about 50 feet (15\xc2\xa0m) wide by about 100 feet (30\xc2\xa0m) long and could support the combined weight of a fueled\n       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">\n        launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">\n        payload\n       </a>\n       and customer-provided launch mount up to about 132,000 pounds (60,000\xc2\xa0kg), and an umbilical tower structure, fluid lines, cables and umbilical arms weighing up to about 47,000 pounds (21,000\xc2\xa0kg).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       GSDO also developed a universal propellant servicing system to provide liquid oxygen and liquid methane fueling capabilities for a variety of small class rockets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       "This is absolutely great to designate a new pad within the confines of Pad 39B. I\'m looking forward to having customers here in the not too distant future, making use of this outstanding facility,"\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Cabana" title="Robert D. Cabana">\n        Robert D. Cabana\n       </a>\n       said\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Capabilities_2">\n        Capabilities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Capabilities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       KSC\xe2\x80\x99s newest Launch Pad, designated 39C, is designed to accommodate Small Class Vehicles. Located in the southeast area of the Launch Complex 39B perimeter, this new concrete pad measures about 50 feet (15\xc2\xa0m) wide by about 100 feet (30\xc2\xa0m) long. Launch Complex 39C will serve as a multi-purpose site allowing companies to test vehicles and capabilities in the smaller class of rockets, making it more affordable for smaller companies to break into the commercial spaceflight market.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As part of this capability, NASA\xe2\x80\x99s Ground Systems Development and Operations Program developed a universal propellant servicing system, which can provide liquid oxygen and liquid methane fueling capabilities for a variety of small class rockets. This system is slated for operational readiness in the summer of 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C_8-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the addition of Launch Complex 39C, KSC can offer the following processing and launching features for companies working with small class vehicles (maximum thrust up to 200,000 pounds-force (890\xc2\xa0kN)):\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C-2_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Processing facilities \xe2\x80\x93 i.e.\n        <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n         Vehicle Assembly Building\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Vehicle/payload transportation (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KAMAG" title="KAMAG">\n         KAMAG\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flatbed_trucks" title="Flatbed trucks">\n         flatbed trucks\n        </a>\n        , tugs, etc.) from integration facility to pad\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Launch site\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Universal propellant servicing system (LOX, LCH4)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Launch_control_center" title="Launch control center">\n         Launch control center\n        </a>\n        /mobile command center options.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lc39C-2_71-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-lc39C-2-71">\n          [71]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">\n        Gallery\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:15px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enterprise_KSC_1979.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2314" data-file-width="1828" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Enterprise_KSC_1979.jpg/95px-Enterprise_KSC_1979.jpg"     </i>\n           </a>\n           on pad 39A during the fit check tests (1979)\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a class="image" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Space_shuttles_Atlantis_%28STS-125%29_and_Endeavour_%28STS-400%29_on_launch_pads_again.jpg/240px-Space_shuttles_Atlantis_%28STS-125%29_and_Endeavour_%28STS-400%29_on_launch_pads_again.jpg 2x" width="120"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Space Shuttles\n           <i>\n            Atlantis\n           </i>\n           and\n           <i>\n            Endeavour\n           </i>\n           are placed at LC39A and LC39B in preparation for the\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n            final service mission\n           </a>\n           to the\n           <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n            Hubble Space Telescope\n           </a>\n           (May 2009).\n           <i>\n            Endeavour\n           </i>\n           was ready for a\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-400" title="STS-400">\n            contingency mission\n           </a>\n           in case of trouble with\n           <i>\n            Atlantis\n           </i>\n           .\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:15px auto;">\n           <a class="image" <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Removal of the top floor of the fixed service structure on LC39B (March 2011)\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">\n        <div style="width: 155px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">\n          <div style="margin:35px auto;">\n           <a      </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           Storage tank for liquid hydrogen fuel located just to the Northeast of Kennedy Space Center\'s former
